text:
I steamed the carrots instead of boiling them.  Instead of turning the heat to low after adding the sauce ingredients, I recommend turning the heat up a bit and cooking until the sauce reduces and carmelizes...just be sure to stir it frequently to keep it from burning.  This way all the good sauce stays on the carrots instead of in the pan.  I also added a pinch of crushed red pepper...I like a sweet/hot combination.  Really very good!

text:
These carrots are wonderful. I sliced carrots on the diagonal about 1/4 inch thick, plunged them in salted boiling water for about 2 minutes, drained, then tossed them in a fry pan that had the butter and sugar already melted together. I cooked another minute or two, seasoned with the salt and pepper and they were good to go with just a slight crunch to them! Fast and fabulous. My dinner guests begged for the recipe!

text:
I came across this recipe because I was looking for a "twist" on an old classic.  I have been making candied carrots similar to these for all of my 47 years as did my mother before me and my grandmother before her.   These are a staple in my house at the very least on Thanksgiving, Christmas and Easter as they go deliciously with the Easter ham.

I use either baby carrots or regular carrots sliced 1/2" to 3/4" thick.  I also tend to use a lot more butter and a little more brown sugar and cook them a bit more to reduce the sauce just a tad.  You can also add a little bit of cinnamon and ground cloves or try adding maple syrup instead of the brown sugar.

For a lower calorie version (and since I have a daughter who is a diabetic), you can cut the butter by half and use orange juice or something similar.  You can also substitute sugar free maple syrup for the brown sugar.

text:
Tasty and sweet and easy to make!  For a potluck gathering I cut up approximately 4 lbs of carrots and made 4 times the sauce.  Cooked the carrots just to the point I could pierce with a fork, drained and set aside in my dutch oven.  Cooked the sauce separately, poured over carrots, covered and let them sit for a couple hours while I worked on other dishes.  Hour before dinner put them in the oven at low heat and then broiled for 5 - 10 minutes stirring often.  I drained the sauce and served, they were sweet and perfect and not mushy at all!  (Sauce is great to keep in the pot too if you like!!)

text:
Really tender and fabulous. As per another reviewer, I steamed rather than boiled the carrots, which took 7 minutes (rather than 20-30). This keeps the flavor as well as the nutrients in. Then, since we were out of brown sugar, I used 1/4 cup of maple syrup  with the butter and put that on med-high heat, and cooked the mixture down until it became a syrup, surrounding the carrots (about 7 minutes). They were perfect! Tender, flavorful, and almost like dessert. A great way to eat your veggies!

text:
I have actually made these carrots twice, but forgot to post my review. I cut the larger size baby carrots in half length-wise, and after bringing water to a boil, I then reduced the heat to medium (not a simmer), and cooked the carrots for 10 minutes. To glaze the carrots I used 2 tablespoons of butter, 1/4 cup of (dark) brown sugar, 2 pinches of salt, a pinch of pepper, and I also added 2 pinches of powdered ginger, which I then cooked (glazed the carrots) for 3 minutes. Enjoyed the carrots, will make again, and next time I may just add another pinch of ground ginger.

Wow!  I would have been making this for YEARS now had I realized how simple it is. I love that this recipe is not cloyingly sweet too - the carrot is the star of the dish here, not the candied coating. I doubled the recipe, using a 2 lb bag of baby carrots from the convenience section of my market. My only substitution was that I used 1/4 C brown sugar + 1/4 local honey in lieu of the 1/2 C sugar I would have used since I was doubling.

EASY recipe and great with strong meats (had it with venision).  You can decide which sweetener you want to use; I used honey with a touch of molasses. text:
These were delicious. I used baby carrots and cooked them covered in the microwave on high with 2 tbsp water for about 6 or 7 minutes. Check every minute until the carrots get to the tenderness you like. While they were cooking I melted the butter in a skillet and added the brown sugar & salt. Cooked on low just long enough to dissolve the sugar. When the carrots were tender I put them in the skillet and warmed them for a couple of minutes. They turned out perfectly.
